INC-SOURCE (P-LI7)  65 MeV proton beam strikes 3 mm thick         22880  1   25 
             natural lithium target. Proton current is 12 micro-A 22880  1   26 
             producing aprx. 1.0E+5 neutrons/cm2/sec at the       22880  1   27 
             location of the target                               22880  1   28 
INC-SPECT   Full width at half maximum is aprx. 2 MeV containing  22880  1   29 
            90% of neutrons/MeV plus a flat continuum of          22880  1   30 
            low-energy neutrons.                                  22880  1   31 
           -For energy calibration the proton and deuteron recoi- 22880  1   32 
            ling from respectively a polypropylene (1 mm thick)   22880  1   33 
            and deuterated polypropylene target (0.6 mm thick)    22880  1   34 
            were used.                                            22880  1   35 
DETECTOR   (TELES,SCIN,CSICR)  Four charged particles detector    22880  1   36 
            consisting of six telescopes were used simultaneously,22880  1   37 
            each of them consists of                              22880  1   38 
             1.  'Delta-E' Detector NE102 plastic scintillator,   22880  1   39 
                  0.1 mm thick, 4 cm diameter, and                22880  1   40 
             2.   Cs-I(Tl) 'E' detector, crystal 22 mm thick,     22880  1   41 
                  38.1 mm diameter                                22880  1   42 
METHOD     (TOF)  The time-of-flight method was deduced from the  22880  1   43 
              time difference between the capacitive beam pickoff 22880  1   44 
              located upstream from the neutron-producing target, 22880  1   45 
              and the delta-E detector. Only those events of      22880  1   46 
              charged particles detection  were registered which  22880  1   47 
              are associated with neutrons in the main neutron    22880  1   48 
              peak.                                               22880  1   49 
           (COINC,EDE)                                            22880  1   50 
MONITOR    (1-H-1(N,EL)1-H-1,,DA)   Cross Sections were Measured  22880  1   51 
             at degrees between 20 and 70 degree with step 10 deg 22880  1   52 
             in each of the telescopes                            22880  1   53 
SAMPLE      Square metallic bismuth 6*6 cm2, 0.315 mm thick.      22880  1   54 
            Purity 99.99%, density 9.831 gram/cm3                 22880  1   55 
CORRECTION .The solid angle and thick target corrections were     22880  1   56 
            made with the help of Monte Carlo simulation program  22880  1   57 
ADD-RES    (THEO)  Multistep direct models of Feshbach-Kerman-    22880  1   58 
                   Koonin, Distorted Wave Born Approximation and  22880  1   59

                  Comparison with theoretical calculations based  22880  1   61

            absolute scale due to:                                22880  1   65

                  cross sections (5%),                            22880  1   67

           (ERR-3,2.,5.) uncertainty in the statistics in the     22880  1   69 
           H(n,p) recoil proton peak (2-5%),                      22880  1   70 
           (ERR-4) uncertainty in solid angle corrections (1%),   22880  1   71 
           (ERR-5) uncertainty in number of target nuclei, etc.   22880  1   72 
           (DATA-ERR,5.5,) The overall relative uncertainties of  22880  1   73 
           the experimental points in the spectra are about 6.%,  22880  1   74 
           9.%, 20.% and 25% for respectively p, d, t and alpha at22880  1   75 
           62.7 MeV. They are mainly given by the statistics in   22880  1   76 
           the spectra. At lower ejectile energies, the thick     22880  1   77 
           target corrections contribute with supplementary       22880  1   78 
           uncertainties. For all the other incident neutron      22880  1   79 
           energies (continuum), these values are between 2 and 3 22880  1   80 
           times higher as a consequence of the lower incident    22880  1   81
